## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (classical mechanics) — nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration and the features are position x, velocity v, and time t, which matches second-order ODE models of (possibly driven/damped) nonlinear harmonic oscillators where dv_dt = f(x, v, t) encodes restoring forces, damping/friction, and external or parametric forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear (Hookean) oscillator (conservative): dv_dt = -c0 * x (small-amplitude linear restoring force)
- Constant bias/tilt (shifted equilibrium): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 (gravity-like constant acceleration component)
- Viscously damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (linear damping proportional to velocity)
- Time-varying linear damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - (c1 + c2 * t) * v (slowly changing dissipation)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Driven damped oscillator (cosine phase): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (same with phase shift)
- Duffing oscillator (hardening/softening spring): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (cubic stiffness nonlinearity)
- Higher-order polynomial restoring force: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) - c3 * v (stronger anharmonic potential)
- Amplitude-dependent stiffness (nonsmooth hardening): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * Abs(x)) * x - c2 * v (piecewise/impact-like stiffness growth)
- Quadratic (aerodynamic) drag damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v * Abs(v) (drag dominates at large |v|)
- Coulomb-like dry friction regularized: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v / (Abs(v) + c3) (approximately constant-magnitude friction near large |v|)
- Van der Pol oscillator (self-excited, limit cycle): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (negative damping at small |x|, positive at large |x|)
- Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (damping changes sign with speed; can create self-oscillation)
- Parametric excitation (time-modulated stiffness): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (Mathieu-like behavior, parametric resonance)
- State-coupled forcing/feedback: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * x * v (nonlinear coupling that can model feedback or nonconservative effects)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring forces typically appear as odd functions of x (e.g., -c*x, -c*x**3), reflecting symmetry of the potential about equilibrium.
- Linear viscous damping is proportional to v and always opposes motion (term -c*v); if the fitted coefficient flips sign, it suggests active forcing/self-excitation.
- Hardening vs softening stiffness is indicated by the sign of the x**3 term in dv_dt: negative coefficient on x**3 increases frequency with amplitude (hardening), positive tends to soften.
- Self-excited limit cycles often require state-dependent damping such as (1 - c*x**2)*v or v - c*v**3, producing energy injection at small amplitude and dissipation at large amplitude.
- External periodic driving usually enters additively as sin(c*t) or cos(c*t); its presence is suggested by dv_dt depending on t even when x and v are small.
- Parametric resonance is suggested by multiplicative time dependence with x (e.g., x*cos(c*t)), i.e., time-modulated stiffness rather than additive forcing.
- Dry friction produces a near-discontinuity around v = 0; in smooth symbolic regression it often appears as v/(Abs(v)+c) or tanh(c*v) (regularized sign).
- Quadratic drag manifests as v*Abs(v), becoming negligible at small |v| but dominating damping at large |v|, leading to strongly amplitude-dependent decay rates.
- If dv_dt depends only on x (no v, no t), the system is effectively conservative (no dissipation/forcing) and trajectories conserve an energy-like invariant.
- Coupling terms like x*v can indicate nonconservative feedback or coordinate-dependent damping (e.g., geometric or control-induced effects).

GT Equivalence Verification (PO37)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - c1*beta*v - omega0**c2*(gamma*t + c3)*x
Candidate formulas: 55

GT (fixed) is:
\[
0.719321236251799\sin(t)\;-\;1.91960248272986\,v\;-\;0.0856781567252997\,v^3\;-\;1.73029531320599\,x\,(0.0808213006269486\,t+1).
\]
Expand the \(x\)-term:
\[
-1.73029531320599\,x\;-\;(1.73029531320599\cdot 0.0808213006269486)\,t x
\]
and \(1.73029531320599\cdot 0.0808213006269486 \approx 0.139858\).  
So GT is exactly of the form:
\[
(A)\sin(t) + (B)v + (C)v^3 + (D)x + (E)tx
\]
with no constants, no other nonlinearities, and sine argument exactly \(t\) (up to phase/frequency choices).

Thus any candidate can match if it can be reduced (by setting free parameters) to:
- one sine term with argument \(t\) (or phase-shifted but still frequency 1),
- linear \(v\),
- cubic \(v^3\),
- linear \(x\),
- \(t x\),
- and all extra terms set to 0.

Now check candidates:

1. \(c0*x + c1*v + c2\sin(c3+c4 t)+c5 v^3 + c6 tx + c7 v(c8+t)^{c9}\).  
Set \(c7=0\). Choose \(c4=1,c3=0\) to get \(\sin(t)\). Then pick \(c2=0.7193\), \(c1=-1.9196\), \(c5=-0.085678\), \(c0=-1.730295\), \(c6=-0.139858\). Works. **Match**.

2. Same as (1) but has extra \(+v^3\). Then total cubic coefficient is \(c5+1\). Set \(c7=0\) and choose \(c5=-1.0856781567\) so \(c5 v^3+v^3=-0.085678 v^3\). Other parameters as in (1). **Match**.

3. \(c0 x+c1 v+c2\sin(c3 t+c4)+c5\sin(c6+c7 t)+c8 v^3+c9 tx+v^3\).  
Need only one sine: set \(c5=0\). Make \(\sin(c3 t+c4)=\sin(t)\) via \(c3=1,c4=0\). Cubic: \(c8+1=-0.085678\Rightarrow c8=-1.085678\). Set \(c0,c1,c9\) to match \(x,v,tx\). **Match**.

4. Same as (3) but without extra \(+v^3\). Set \(c5=0\), set \(c3=1,c4=0\), set \(c8=-0.085678\), and match \(c0,c1,c9\). **Match**.

5. Adds \(c5 e^{c6 t}\) and constant \(c9\). To match GT (no such terms), set \(c5=0\) and \(c9=0\). Remaining terms can match as in (1). **Match**.

6. Adds \(c5 x^{c6}\) and constant \(c9\). Set \(c5=0\), \(c9=0\). Remaining match. **Match**.

7. Has \(c0 x + \dots + c7 x + c8 + v^3\). Combine \(x\)-terms: \((c0+c7)x\). Set \(c8=0\). Cubic: \(c5+1=-0.085678\Rightarrow c5=-1.085678\). Choose sine and \(v,tx\) as before; choose \(c0+c7=-1.730295\). **Match**.

8. Like (7) but no extra \(+v^3\). Set \(c8=0\). Choose \(c5=-0.085678\). Choose \(c0+c7=-1.730295\). Others match. **Match**.

9. \(c0 x + c1 v + c2 v + c3 + c4\sin(c5+c6 t)+c7 v^3 + c8 tx + v^3\).  
Linear \(v\) coefficient is \(c1+c2\). Set constant \(c3=0\). Sine: set \(c6=1,c5=0\), \(c4=0.7193\). Cubic: \(c7+1=-0.085678\Rightarrow c7=-1.085678\). Set \(c0=-1.730295\), \(c8=-0.139858\), and \(c1+c2=-1.919602\). **Match**.
